      <p>The <b>Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe Party</b> (<b>ALDE Party</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European political party</a> composed of 60 national-level <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> parties from across Europe, mainly active in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. On 26 March 1976, it was founded in <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a> as a confederation of national political parties under the name <b>Federation of Liberal and Democrat Parties in Europe</b> and renamed <b>European Liberals and Democrats</b> (<b>ELD</b>) in 1977 and <b>European Liberal Democrats and Reformists</b> (<b>ELDR</b>) in 1986. On 30 April 2004, the ELDR was reformed as an official European party, the <b>European Liberal Democrat and Reform Party</b> (<b>ELDR Party</b>).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The ALDE Party is affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_International" title="Liberal International">Liberal International</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> and a recognised European political party, incorporated as a non-profit association under <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Belgium" title="Law of Belgium">Belgian law</a>. </p>
      <p>On 10 November 2012, the party chose its current name of ALDE Party, taken from its then-<a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_groups_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Political groups of the European Parliament">group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe Group">Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe</a> (ALDE), which had been formed on 20 July 2004 in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/European_Democratic_Party" title="European Democratic Party">European Democratic Party</a> (EDP). Prior to the <a href="/wiki/2004_European_Parliament_election" title="2004 European Parliament election">2004 European election</a> the European party had been represented through its own group, the <a href="/wiki/European_Liberal_Democrat_and_Reform_Party_Group" title="European Liberal Democrat and Reform Party Group">European Liberal Democrat and Reform Party</a> (ELDR) Group. In June 2019, the ALDE group was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Renew_Europe" title="Renew Europe">Renew Europe</a>. </p>
      <p>As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe_Party&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, ALDE is represented in European Union institutions, with 81 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEPs</a> and four members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>. Of the 28 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Member states of the European Union">EU member states</a>, there are six with ALDE-affiliated Prime Ministers: <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rutte" title="Mark Rutte">Mark Rutte</a> (<a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_for_Freedom_and_Democracy" title="People's Party for Freedom and Democracy">VVD</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xavier_Bettel" title="Xavier Bettel">Xavier Bettel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Luxembourg)" title="Democratic Party (Luxembourg)">DP</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCri_Ratas" title="Jüri Ratas">Jüri Ratas</a> (<a href="/wiki/Estonian_Centre_Party" title="Estonian Centre Party">Estonian Centre Party</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Michel" title="Charles Michel">Charles Michel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mouvement_R%C3%A9formateur" title="Mouvement Réformateur">MR</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marjan_%C5%A0arec" title="Marjan Šarec">Marjan Šarec</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_Marjan_%C5%A0arec" title="List of Marjan Šarec">LMS</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andrej_Babi%C5%A1" title="Andrej Babiš">Andrej Babiš</a> (<a href="/wiki/ANO_2011" title="ANO 2011">ANO</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>. Liberals are also in government in three other EU member states: <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>. </p>
      <p>ALDE's think tank is the <a href="/wiki/European_Liberal_Forum" title="European Liberal Forum">European Liberal Forum</a>. The youth wing of ALDE is the <a href="/wiki/European_Liberal_Youth" title="European Liberal Youth">European Liberal Youth</a> (LYMEC), which is predominantly based upon youth and student liberal organisations but contains also a small number of individual members. LYMEC is led by Vedrana Gujic (<a href="/wiki/Croatian_People%27s_Party_%E2%80%93_Liberal_Democrats" title="Croatian People's Party – Liberal Democrats">HNS</a>, Croatia), who was elected for a two-year term as LYMEC President in May 2014, and counts 200,000 members. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bureau">Bureau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Bureau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_pan-European_liberalism">History of pan-European liberalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History of pan-European liberalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_pan-European_liberalism" title="History of pan-European liberalism">History of pan-European liberalism</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ELDR_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/ELDR_logo.svg/150px-ELDR_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="86" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/ELDR_logo.svg/225px-ELDR_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/ELDR_logo.svg/300px-ELDR_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="417" data-file-height="240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ELDR_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>ELDR Party logo (2009–2012).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Pan-European liberalism has a long history dating back to the foundation of Liberal International in April 1947. On 26 March 1976, the Federation of Liberal and Democrat Parties in Europe was established in <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>. The founding parties of the federation were the <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_(Germany)" title="Free Democratic Party (Germany)">Free Democratic Party</a> of Germany, <a href="/wiki/Radical_Party_(France)" title="Radical Party (France)">Radical Party</a> of France, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(Denmark)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal Party (Denmark)">Liberal Party</a> of Denmark, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Liberal_Party" title="Italian Liberal Party">Italian Liberal Party</a>, Dutch <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_for_Freedom_and_Democracy" title="People's Party for Freedom and Democracy">People's Party for Freedom and Democracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Luxembourg)" title="Democratic Party (Luxembourg)">Democratic Party</a> of Luxembourg.<sup id="cite_ref-Almeida2012_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Almeida2012-6">[6]</a></sup> Observer members joining later in 1976 were the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Social_Liberal_Party" title="Danish Social Liberal Party">Danish Social Liberal Party</a>, French <a href="/wiki/Radical_Party_of_the_Left" title="Radical Party of the Left">Radical Party of the Left</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independent_Republicans" title="Independent Republicans">Independent Republicans</a>, British <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal Party</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Republican_Party" title="Italian Republican Party">Italian Republican Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Almeida2012_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Almeida2012-6">[6]</a></sup> In 1977, the federation was renamed European Liberals and Democrats, in 1986, European Liberal Democrats and Reformists. </p>
      <p>It evolved into the European Liberal Democrat and Reform Party (ELDR Party) in 2004, when it was founded as an official <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European party</a> under that name and incorporated under Belgian law at an extraordinary Congress in Brussels, held on 30 April 2004 the day before the <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">enlargement of the European Union</a>. At the same time the matching group in the European Parliament, the <a href="/wiki/European_Liberal_Democrat_and_Reform_Party_(European_Parliament_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="European Liberal Democrat and Reform Party (European Parliament group)">European Liberal Democrats and Reformists</a> Group allied with the members of the newly elected <a href="/wiki/European_Democratic_Party" title="European Democratic Party">European Democratic Party</a>, forming the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe" title="Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe">Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe</a> (ALDE) with a matching <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe Group">ALDE Group in the European Parliament</a>. </p>
      <p>On 10 November 2012, the ELDR Party adopted the name of the alliance between the two parties, in order to match the parliamentary group and the alliance. </p>
      <p>On 12 June 2019, the ALDE group was succeeded by a new, enlarged group <a href="/wiki/Renew_Europe" title="Renew Europe">Renew Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
